The Principle of Specific over General in Intercession
Discussion of preference for specific proofs over general in intercession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the principle of preferring specific evidence over general evidence supports the Sunni position on intercession.

Core Idea
Specific proofs outweigh general proofs in the debate on intercession.

This passage presents a key methodological argument from Imam al-Razi. When debating intercession, the Mu'tazilites used general proofs to deny it, while the Sunnis used specific proofs to affirm it. The principle of usul al-fiqh that the specific takes precedence over the general gives the Sunni position logical strength. Let's explore this concise argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice that the passage includes a direct quote from Imam al-Razi.
2
Identify the two types of proofs
The passage contrasts the Mu'tazilite proofs (general in persons and times) with the Sunni proofs (specific in both). Underline or note these descriptions.
The terms 'عام' (general) and 'خاص' (specific) are key.
3
Understand the rule of precedence
Al-Razi states that 'الخاص مقدم على العام' (the specific is given precedence over the general). Reflect on why this rule would make the Sunni argument stronger.
This is a well-known principle in usul al-fiqh.
4
Consider the implication
Because the Sunni proofs are specific and the Mu'tazilite proofs are general, the specific outweighs the general, so the preponderance (الترجيح) is with the Sunnis.
This does not mean intercession is absolutely universal; it is limited to certain persons and times.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النفي فتكون عامة وإن كانت واردة على سبب خاص، والإمام الرازي بعدما أورد شبهات المعتزلة في إثبات ما ادعوه قال : والجواب عنها إجمالاً أن يقال : دلائلكم في نفي الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون عامة في الأشخاص والأوقات ودلائلنا في إثباتها لا بد أن تكون خاصة فيهما لأنا لا نثبت الشفاعة في حق كل شخص ولا في جميع الأوقات والخاص مقدم على العام فالترجيح معنا وأما الأجوبة المفصلة فمذكورة في التفسير الكبير.
The negation is general even if it is based on a specific cause. Imam al-Razi, after presenting the doubts of the Mu'tazilites in proving what they claimed, said: The answer to them in summary is to say: your proofs for the negation of intercession (al-shafa'a) must be general with respect to persons and times, while our proofs for its affirmation must be specific with respect to them, because we do not affirm intercession for every person nor at all times. The specific (al-khass) is given precedence over the general (al-'amm), so the preponderance is with us. As for detailed answers, they are mentioned in al-Tafsir al-Kabir.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage presents a summary argument for the Sunni position on intercession (al-shafa'a). It begins by stating a rule: a general negation (from a specific cause) remains general. Then it quotes Imam al-Razi's approach in refuting the Mu'tazilite arguments against intercession. The method is to note that the opponents' proofs for denying intercession are general in scope (applying to all persons and times), whereas the Sunni proofs for affirming intercession are specific (limited to certain persons and times). Since specific evidence takes precedence over general evidence, the Sunni position is stronger. This illustrates an important principle in usul al-fiqh: the specific is given precedence over the general when they conflict. The passage also refers to detailed answers in al-Razi's Tafsir al-Kabir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Correction: The passage clarifies that intercession is specific to certain persons and times, not universal in scope.

Checkpoint

B) Because specific evidence outweighs general evidence
C) Because the Mu'tazilites ignore tradition
D) Because intercession is only for sinners

Key Takeaway
The Sunni argument for intercession is stronger because it relies on specific evidence, which takes precedence over the general evidence of the Mu'tazilites.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Do you have the courage to hold both the general and the specific in tension, or do you prefer the simplicity of the absolute?

Think of a time when you judged someone's spiritual state based on a general rule without considering the specific circumstances or divine mercy. How might al-Razi's principle of specific over general transform your attitude toward others' shortcomings?
?
You know that intercession is specific, not universal. Does that make you complacent or more earnest in seeking the means to be among those included? Are you actively pursuing the specific conditions that would make intercession apply to you, or are you relying on a vague hope?

The Revival of the Dead in Graves: A Core Belief of Ahl al-Haqq
The author states the belief in revival, questioning, and punishment in the grave as true.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the doctrine of revival in the grave, the questioning by Munkar and Nakir, and the punishment of the grave as affirmed by Ahl al-Haqq, including the nuanced position on the soul's return.

Core Idea
Grave revival is a partial life for reward and punishment, not requiring the soul's full return.

This passage presents the eleventh observation on eschatological matters. The author affirms that revival, questioning, and punishment in the grave are true, agreed upon by the early community and the majority. However, a key nuance emerges: the life in the grave is partial, sufficient for experiencing pain and pleasure, and Ahl al-Haqq hesitate about the return of the soul itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation, noting the three components: revival, Munkar and Nakir questioning, and grave punishment.
The passage uses strong language: 'all are true according to us'.
2
Understand the consensus
Notice that the author emphasizes agreement by the Salaf and the majority, implying these doctrines are well-established.
3
Examine the nuance on the soul
The passage explains that Ahl al-Haqq hesitate (tawaqqafū) about the soul's return. They deny that life is impossible without the soul in this context.
This is a key distinctive point.
4
Reflect on the partial life
Understand that grave life is a type of life (nawʿ ḥayāt) for feeling pain and pleasure, not complete life with voluntary actions.
The passage ends with 'but it is problematic' indicating further discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الحادي عشر : إحياء الموتى في القبور. إحياء الموتى في قبورهم ومسألة منكر ونكير لهم وعذاب القبر للكافر والفاسق كلها حق عندنا واتفق عليه سلف الأمة قبل ظهور الخلاف واتفق عليه الأكثر. قوله : إحياء الموتى في قبورهم اتفق أهل الحق على أن الله تعالى يعيد إلى الميت في القبر نوع حياة قدر ما يتألم ويتلذذ لكن توقفوا في عود الروح وما يتوهم من امتناع الحياة بدون الروح ممنوع ، وإنما ذلك في الحياة الكاملة التي معها القدرة على الأفعال الاختيارية لكن يشكل
The Eleventh Observation: The Revival of the Dead in Graves. The revival of the dead in their graves, the question of Munkar and Nakir for them, and the punishment of the grave for the disbeliever and the sinner – all of these are true according to us, and the predecessors of the community agreed upon before the emergence of disagreement, and the majority agreed upon it. His statement: 'The revival of the dead in their graves' – Ahl al-Haqq agreed that God restores to the dead in the grave a type of life to the extent of feeling pain and pleasure, but they hesitated regarding the return of the soul. What is imagined of the impossibility of life without the soul is denied. Rather, that (dependence on the soul) applies only to complete life that includes ability for voluntary actions, but it is problematic...
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage addresses the eleventh observation: revival of the dead in graves. The author affirms that revival, the questioning by Munkar and Nakir, and grave punishment for disbelievers and sinners are true, agreed upon by the salaf and the majority. A commentary explains that Ahl al-Haqq agree on a partial life for experiencing pain/pleasure but disagree on the return of the soul. They deny that life is impossible without the soul; that only holds for full life with voluntary actions.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Revival in the grave requires the full return of the soul for voluntary actions.
Correction: Ahl al-Haqq affirm a partial life without the full return of the soul, sufficient only for experiencing pain and pleasure.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Haqq affirm a partial life in the grave for reward and punishment, without requiring the soul's full return for voluntary actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The First Proof: Punishment of the Grave from Quran 40:46
Al-Iji presents the first proof from Quran 40:46 and refutes opposing views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Quran 40:46 proves the punishment of the grave and why it necessarily implies revivification and questioning.

Core Idea
The Quranic evidence for the grave's punishment is explicit, and it logically entails life and questioning.

Al-Iji begins his defense of the punishment of the grave by citing a powerful Quranic proof. The verse about Pharaoh's people distinguishes a pre-Resurrection punishment from the final punishment, which is identified as the torment of the grave. This passage not only presents the proof but also draws out its necessary implications and refutes alternative interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. Notice how the author structures his argument: first citing the verse, then deriving the implication, then addressing objections.
Pay attention to the conjunction 'عطف' which is key to his reasoning.
2
Understand the Quranic proof
Identify how the verse shows two distinct punishments: exposure to Fire morning and evening (before Resurrection) and the severe punishment on the Day of Judgment. The conjunction proves they are separate, and the first is the punishment of the grave.
The verse is Ghafir 40:46.
3
Grasp the necessary implications
Once the punishment of the grave is established, it logically requires that the dead are alive (revivification) and are questioned. The author notes this is a consensus among those who affirm grave punishment.
Abu al-Hudhayl and Bishr used this to argue for punishment between the two blasts.
4
Examine the refuted objections
The author refutes two views: (1) punishment without life (inanimate objects feel nothing), and (2) pains accumulating without sensation until resurrection (denies real pre-Resurrection punishment). Understand why they are invalid.
The second view is attributed to some theologians.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لنا) في إثبات ما هو حق عندنا ( وجهان. الأول: قوله تعالى : النار يعرضون عليها غدواً وعشياً ويوم تقوم الساعة ادخلوا آل فرعون أشد العذاب [غافر : ٤٦] ، عطف، في هذه الآية ( عذاب القيامة عليه ) أي على العذاب الذي هو عرض النار صباحاً ومساءً ( فعلم أنه غيره، ولا شبهة في كونه قبل الإنشار من القبور كما يدل عليه نظم الآية بصريحه (و) ما هو كذلك (ليس غير عذاب القبر اتفاقاً)، لأن الآية وردت في حق الموتى ( فهو هو وبه ) أي ما ذكر من الآية ( ذهب أبو الهذيل العلاف وبشر بن المعتمر إلى أن الكافر يعذب فيما بين النفختين أيضاً، وإذا ثبت التعذيب ثبت الإحياء والمسألة لأن كل من قال بعذاب القبر قال بهما . ( وأما ما ذهب إليه الصالحي من المعتزلة وابن جرير الطبري وطائفة من الكرامية من تجويز ذلك ) التعذيب على الموتى من غير إحياء فخروج عن المعقول)، لأن الجماد لا له فكيف يتصور تعذيبه؟ وما ذهب إليه بعض المتكلمين من أن الآلام تجتمع في أجساد الموتى وتتضاعف من غير إحساس بها فإذا حشروا أحسوا بها دفعة واحدة فهو إنكار للعذاب قبل الحشر فيبطل بما قررناه من ثبوته قبله.
For us, in establishing what is true according to us, there are two aspects. The first: His statement, exalted be He: 'The Fire, they are exposed to it morning and evening, and on the Day the Hour is established, [it will be said], "Admit the family of Pharaoh to the severest punishment." [Ghafir 40:46]. There is a conjunction in this verse of the punishment of the Resurrection upon it, i.e., upon the punishment which is the exposure to the Fire morning and evening. So it is known that it is other than it, and there is no doubt that it is before the resurrection from the graves, as indicated by the wording of the verse explicitly. And what is like that is not other than the punishment of the grave by agreement, because the verse came concerning the dead. So it is it. And by it, i.e., what was mentioned from the verse, Abu al-Hudhayl al-'Allaf and Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir held that the disbeliever is punished between the two blasts as well. And if the punishment is established, then the revivification and the questioning are established, because everyone who said there is punishment of the grave said them both. As for what went to al-Salihi from the Mu'tazila, Ibn Jarir al-Tabari, and a group of the Karramiyya of permitting that punishment upon the dead without revivification, it is outside of reason, because the inanimate has no feeling, so how can its punishment be imagined? And what some theologians went to, that pains accumulate in the bodies of the dead and multiply without sensation, then when they are resurrected they feel them all at once, is a denial of the punishment before the resurrection, and it is invalidated by what we have established of its existence before it.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof for the punishment of the grave. The author begins by stating there are two proofs; this is the first. He cites Quran 40:46, which mentions the people of Pharaoh being exposed to the Fire morning and evening, and then on the Day of Resurrection they are admitted to the severest punishment. The author explains that the verse conjoins the punishment of the Resurrection to the exposure to the Fire, showing that the exposure is something else. He argues that this exposure occurs before the resurrection from the graves, as the verse's wording indicates. Since it is before the Resurrection and applies to the dead, it must be the punishment of the grave, by consensus. He then notes that Abu al-Hudhayl and Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir used this verse to prove that the disbeliever is punished between the two trumpet blasts, and that punishment implies revivification and questioning. Next, he refutes two opposing views: (1) that punishment can occur without life—rejected because inanimate objects feel no pain; (2) that pains accumulate without sensation until resurrection—rejected because it denies real punishment before the resurrection. Thus the proof establishes punishment, revivification, and questioning in the grave.

Key Terms

الإحياء
المسألة
النفختان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That punishment of the grave can occur without life or revivification.
Correction: The passage refutes this by stating that inanimate objects have no feeling, so punishment without life is irrational. Punishment of the grave necessarily implies that the dead are alive and conscious.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the conjunction in Quran 40:46 indicate?
A) The exposure to Fire is the same as the punishment of the Resurrection
B) The exposure to Fire is a different punishment occurring before the Resurrection
C) The exposure to Fire occurs after the Resurrection
D) The punishment of the grave is metaphorical

Key Takeaway
Quran 40:46 provides explicit evidence for the punishment of the grave, which necessarily entails revivification and questioning, and objections that deny life or real torment are rationally and textually unsound.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The inanimate feel no pain, yet you will be alive in your grave to experience punishment. What have you done today to prepare for that moment? Are you living as if you truly believe this reality starts tonight?
?
This passage refutes the idea that punishment can be delayed or deferred without sensation. How does the immediacy of the grave's torment change the way you think about a single sin you committed this week? Will you repent now, or wait until it is too late?
?
The people of Pharaoh were given a taste of Fire before the final judgment. If you were to die tonight, would you face that same exposure? What specific habit or attachment in your life right now makes you afraid to answer that question honestly?

Unseen Matters
beginner
4 min
The Common Interpretation of the Two Deaths and Two Lives
Al-Iji presents the common interpretation of Quran 40:11.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the common interpretation of Quran 40:11 regarding the two deaths and two lives and how it establishes life in the grave.

Core Idea
The two deaths and two lives in the Quran establish life in the grave.

In this passage, al-Iji presents the second proof for life in the grave from Quran 40:11. He explains the widely accepted interpretation among exegetes: the first death ends worldly life, the first life is in the grave, the second death follows the questioning by Munkar and Nakir, and the second life is at the resurrection. This interpretation is the foundation for belief in the intermediate state.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and the interpretation
Read the Arabic passage once, focusing on the verse and its explanation. Then read the translation to grasp the author's reasoning.
Notice how the author cites the Quran directly.
2
Identify the sequence of deaths and lives
List the four stages mentioned: death before the grave, life in the grave, death after questioning, life at resurrection. Understand their order.
3
Understand the purpose of mentioning the two lives
The exegetes say the two lives show God's power over resurrection, leading to confession of sins.
This connects to the overall argument for life in the grave.
4
Recognize the conclusion
The author concludes that revivification in the grave is established by this interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه ( الثاني : قوله تعالى حكاية على سبيل التصديق ( ربنا أمتنا اثنتين وأحييتنا اثنتين ﴾ [غافر: ۱۱] وما هو أي وما المراد بالإماتتين والإحيائين في هذه الآية ( إلا الإماتة ) قبل مزار القبور ) ثم الإحياء في القبر ثم الإماتة فيه أيضاً بعد مسألة منكر ونكير ) ثم الإحياء للحشر) هذا هو الشائع المستفيض بين أصحاب التفسير قالوا : والغرض بذكر الإحيائين أنهم عرفوا فيهما قدرة الله على البعث ولهذا قالوا : فاعترفنا بذنبونا أي الذنوب التي حصلت بسبب إنكار الحشر، وإنما لم يذكر الإحياء في الدنيا لأنهم لم يكونوا معترفين بذنبوهم في هذا الإحياء في القبر لأن مقصودهم ذكر الأمور الماضية، وأما الحياة الثالثة أعني حياة الحشر فهم فيها فلا حاجة إلى ذكرها وعلى هذين التفسيرين ثبت الإحياء في القبر، ومن قال بالإحياء فيه قال بالمسألة

هذا الجواب لمنكر ونكير على ما ورد في الحديث كذا في شرح المقاصد، وقد يدفع الإشكال بأن الجواب للروح بلا آلة الجسد لأن المكلف بالشرائع هو الروح المدرك وهو مبدأ الأعمال، فلا بد من حضوره عند المجازاة سواء كان يعود إلى البدن أم لا، وأنت خبير بأن الاتفاق المذكور يقتضي أن يكون الجواب بآلة البدن والإشكال مسوق على ذلك، فتأمل.

والعذاب ( أيضاً قد ثبت أن الكل حق وأما حمل الإماتة الأولى على خلقهم أمواتاً أطوار النطفة وحمل الثانية على الإماتة الظاهرة وحمل الإماتتين على إحياء الدنيا والإحياء عند الحشر، وحينئذ لا يثبت بالآية الإحياء في القبر، فقد رد عليه بأن الإماتة إنما تكون بعد سابقة الحياة ولا حياة في أطوار النطف وبأنه قول شذوذ من المفسرين والمعتمد هو قول الأكثرين
The second aspect: His statement, exalted be He, relating in affirmation: 'Our Lord, You made us die twice and gave us life twice' [Ghafir 40:11]. And what is meant by the two deaths and the two lives in this verse is: the death before [entering] the abodes of the graves, then the life in the grave, then the death in it also after the questioning by Munkar and Nakir, then the life for the Resurrection. This is the widespread common view among the exegetes. They said: The purpose of mentioning the two lives is that they recognized in them God's power over the resurrection, and therefore they said: 'So we confess our sins' — i.e., the sins that occurred due to denial of the resurrection. And the life in this world was not mentioned because they were not confessing their sins in this life in the grave, because their purpose was to mention past matters. As for the third life, namely the life of the Resurrection, they are in it, so there is no need to mention it. And upon these two interpretations, revivification in the grave is established, and whoever said revivification in it said the questioning. This is the answer to Munkar and Nakir according to what came in the hadith, thus in Sharh al-Maqasid. And the problem can be repelled by that the answer is for the soul without the instrument of the body, because the one obligated by the laws is the perceiving soul, which is the principle of actions. So its presence is necessary at the requital, whether it returns to the body or not. And you are aware that the mentioned consensus requires that the answer be with the instrument of the body, and the problem is raised concerning that, so reflect. And the punishment also: it has been established that all is true. As for interpreting the first death as their being created dead in the stages of the sperm-drop, and interpreting the second as the apparent death, and interpreting the two deaths as the life of this world and the life at the resurrection — then the revivification in the grave is not established by the verse. But this is refuted because death only occurs after a preceding life, and there is no life in the stages of the sperm-drop, and because it is an odd opinion among the exegetes, while the relied-upon view is the majority view.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof from Quran 40:11. The author cites the verse where the disbelievers say, 'Our Lord, You made us die twice and gave us life twice.' He explains the common interpretation: the first death is the death at the end of worldly life, the first life is life in the grave, the second death after the questioning by Munkar and Nakir, and the second life at the resurrection. This is the widely accepted view of the exegetes. They note that the purpose of mentioning the two lives is to acknowledge God's power over resurrection, as the disbelievers confess their sins for denying the resurrection. The author then adds a note about the response to Munkar and Nakir, discussing whether it is with the body or soul, and points out a consensus issue. Finally, he refutes an alternative interpretation that the first death refers to the state of being a sperm-drop, arguing that death presupposes life, so that interpretation is invalid; the majority view is the relied-upon one.

Key Terms
إماتتان
إحياءان
مسألة منكر ونكير
عذاب القبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the common interpretation, what is the first death?
A) Death before entering the grave
B) Death after the questioning
C) Death at the resurrection
D) Death in the sperm-drop stage

Key Takeaway
The common interpretation of Quran 40:11 establishes that there is life in the grave, followed by a second death after questioning, and then resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to be questioned in your grave right now about your faith and deeds, what would you say? What have you done today that will help you answer confidently?
?
The disbelievers in the verse confessed their sins only after seeing God's power in the two lives. Is there a sin you are still hiding or denying that you need to confess to Allah right now, before you face the grave?
?
You will experience death twice: once at the end of this world and again after the life in the grave. Which death do you fear more? What are you doing to prepare for both?
